The Second Aspect: Two Kinds of Major Sins
Maturidi distinguishes two types of major sins and reinterprets 'avoidance' as avoiding shirk.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's distinction between belief-based major sins and action-based major sins, and how this distinction preserves the possibility of forgiveness for believers who commit sins due to weakness.

Core Idea
Avoiding major sins means avoiding disbelief, not perfection in actions.

In this second aspect, Maturidi provides a deeper analysis of what 'major sins' means. He divides them into two categories: those related to belief (such as shirk) and those related to actions. He argues that the verse's command to 'avoid' refers primarily to belief-based major sins, because a person can avoid those while still occasionally committing action-based sins. This allows for a more nuanced understanding of forgiveness.

Guided Path
1
Read the second aspect from the passage
Read from 'والثاني أن الكبائر نوعان' to the end of the passage. Focus on the two types of major sins and the conclusion.
2
Understand the two types
Major sins in belief: disbelief and denial. Major sins in action: sinful acts that the believer still considers wrong.
The believer who commits action-based sins still 'avoids' them in belief by recognizing their gravity.
3
See Maturidi's reinterpretation
Maturidi says the verse's 'avoidance' likely means avoiding belief-based major sins. This allows the verse to promise forgiveness for other sins (action-based) through good deeds or divine favor.
4
Contrast with Mu'tazilite view
Mu'tazila see any major sin (action or belief) as negating faith. Maturidi argues that action-based sins do not remove one from faith, as long as belief is sound.

Then the verse has aspects that prevent the saying of the Mu'tazila and Khawarij. One of them: He said: 'If you avoid the major sins which you are forbidden' [4:31], and in that there is no clarification of the ruling for one who does not avoid. And the second: that major sins are of two types: one is major sins in belief from the types of disbelief and denial by which the disbelievers differ, and the other is major sins of actions whose doer avoids them by belief in that he sees them as Allah has made them upon him of greatness of the act and sin; and this is avoidance, and he may commit them by action, which is perpetration, and in the verse there is no face of avoidance. Commentary
This passage presents the first two of three aspects that refute the Mu'tazilite and Kharijite interpretations of Quran 4:31. The first aspect: the verse says 'If you avoid the major sins which you are forbidden' but does not specify the ruling for one who does not avoid them. Refutation of the Argument that Sinning Nullifies Initial Faith
Maturidi refutes the argument that sinning proves initial faith was false.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of the claim that committing a major sin proves one's initial declaration of faith was insincere.

Core Idea
A sin does not retroactively falsify faith—Maturidi shows the impossibility of this argument.

Some argued that if a believer later commits a grave sin, it proves they were lying when they first professed faith. Maturidi rejects this as logically impossible and corrupt. In this passage, he presents a counterexample from the nature of intellect and draws out absurd consequences of the opposing view.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once through, then read the literal translation. Let Maturidi's argument unfold without interruption.
The text ends abruptly; focus on the logical flow up to that point.
2
Identify the refuted argument
The opponent claims that 'omission of the act' (sinning) proves falsehood in the initial faith. Note Maturidi's immediate verdict: impossible and corrupt.
This is a typical kalam refutation opening.
3
Follow the analogy with lying
Maturidi compares the necessity of avoiding falsehood in the intellect to the necessity of preserving faith. A lie does not disprove the intellect's truthfulness, similarly a sin does not disprove initial faith.
4
Examine the absurd consequences
If sinning disproved initial faith, then everything that happens after would corrupt the first, leading to no difference between apostate and original disbeliever, and even explicit disbelief wouldn't prove falsehood of first faith.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
5
Consider the two aspects
Maturidi begins to discuss two aspects (wajhan) but the text cuts off. Reflect on how the first aspect—removal of necessity—strengthens his refutation.
The second aspect is missing due to page break.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واستدلال من استدل بترك الفعل على الكذب في الأول محال فاسد، لأن في عقل كل واحد لزوم اتقاء الكذب كما في القبول إبقاؤه. ثم لم يصر وجوده دليلاً على كذب عقله، لما في عقله منعه. وإن تعدى ذلك فمثله في قبول وقت تعديه. ولو كان في ذلك تبيّن لكان كل شيء إذ حل بالأول، يجب فساده وحرمته. ولو كان كذلك لكان لا يجب على المرتد خلاف على الكافر الأصلي؛ بل بتصريح الكفر لا يظهر كذبه في الأول، فكيف فيما فعل؟ ولو كان بذا ذا، فيظهر أيضاً - بإيمان الكافر من بعد أو بتعاطيه ما لا يقبح في العرف - تصديقه على كذبه وأصله وجهان أحدهما لو كان يظهر به الكذب في الأول لأزيل اللزوم، وإذا زال
And the proof of one who proves by the omission of the act upon falsehood in the first [faith] is impossible and corrupt, because in the intellect of every one is the necessity of avoiding falsehood just as in acceptance is its preservation. Then its existence did not become evidence of the falsehood of his intellect, due to what is in his intellect preventing it. And if it transgresses that, then its like is in acceptance at the time of its transgression. And if there were in that a clarification, then everything when it occurs in the first would require its corruption and prohibition. And if that were so, then the apostate would not be required something different from the original disbeliever. Rather, by explicit disbelief, his falsehood does not appear in the first, so how regarding what he did? And if it were like that, then it also appears – by the belief of the disbeliever afterwards or by his doing what is not considered ugly in custom – his confirmation upon his falsehood and his origin: two aspects, one of which is that if falsehood appeared by it in the first, the necessity would be removed, and when it is removed...
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage is a refutation (istidlal) of an argument made by some sect. The opponent argued that committing a major sin (tark al-fi'l, i.e., leaving the required action) proves that one was lying in their first faith (that they were not truly believers). Maturidi calls this argument impossible and corrupt (muhal fasad). He gives a counterexample: in every person's intellect, there is a necessity (luzum) to avoid lying, just as there is a necessity to preserve what is accepted. However, the existence of a lie does not prove that one's intellect is false, because the intellect also has a prohibition against lying. Similarly, committing a sin does not negate the initial sincerity of faith. If transgression occurs, it is like the case of acceptance at the time of transgression – that is, the initial acceptance remains valid. If a sin could clarify that one's first faith was false, then everything that occurs afterward would corrupt the first. That would lead to absurd consequences, such as there being no difference between an apostate and an original disbeliever. Even explicit disbelief (tasrih al-kufr) does not prove that one's earlier faith was false – how then can a mere action? Then he mentions two aspects (wajhan) to further refute the argument, but the text cuts off. The first aspect: if sinning made falsehood appear in the first, the necessity of avoiding it would be removed.

Key Terms
الاستدلال
الكذب في الأول
اللزوم
المرتد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Committing a major sin after accepting Islam proves that one's initial declaration of faith was insincere (a lie).
Correction: Maturidi argues that this is impossible and corrupt; sinning does not retroactively falsify faith, just as telling a lie does not falsify the intellect that prohibits lying.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi refutes the claim that sinning proves initial faith false by logical impossibility and absurd consequences.

If a sin cannot retroactively prove your faith false, then where does your security in faith really lie—in your own deeds or in something else? How does this change how you view your past failures?
?
Maturidi says even explicit disbelief does not prove earlier faith false. Does that challenge your understanding of apostasy? How does this affect the way you judge others who once believed but later struggled? Will you now extend more grace?

Refuting Mu'tazila and Khawarij on Threat Verses
Maturidi refutes Mu'tazila and Khawarij claims by analyzing verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazila and Khawarij claim that threat verses are general, and why the position of waqf (suspension) is necessary.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila and Khawarij cannot claim generality for threat verses without contradicting themselves.

Imam Maturidi responds to two sectarian positions that take Quranic threat verses as unconditional and general. By analyzing their own interpretations of key verses, he demonstrates that they must be specific to disbelief. This leads to the sound position of al-Husayn al-Karābīsī: suspension of judgment (waqf) regarding threats.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its literal English translation. Note the verses cited and the flow of the argument.
2
Identify the key verses and the refutation
Notice the three threat verses and the forgiveness verses. Observe how Maturidi uses them to show that Mu'tazila and Khawarij interpretations reduce all major sins to disbelief.
3
Understand the conclusion
Reflect on why the author concludes that the correct position is waqf (suspension) and that making rulings without evidence is arbitrary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يبين ذلك قوله تعالى: ومن يكفر بالإيمان الآية، وقوله: ومن يبتغ غير الإسلام دينا الآية، وقوله: ومن يرتدد منكم عن دينه الآية، وعلى ذلك تأويل قوله: إن الله لا يغفر أن يشرك به، ثم قال: ويغفر ما دون ذلك لمن يشاء [النساء، ٤٨/٤]؛ كما قال في هذا: ونكفر عنكم سيئاتكم [النساء، ٣١/٤]، فيكون الإتيان بحكم واحد؛ ومعلوم أن لا درك للمعتزلة والخوارج في إحداهما، فكذلك في الأخرى. ثم الأصل أن قوله: إن تجتنبوا كبائر ما تنهون عنه نكفر عنكم سيئاتكم [النساء، ٣١/٤]، على قول الخوارج كأنه قال: إن تجتنبوا الكفر والشرك، وعلى قول المعتزلة: إن تجتنبوا الخروج من الإيمان نكفر عنكم ما ذكر، فلا كبيرة إذن على قولهم إلا الخروج من الإيمان؛ فصارت الآية على قولهم راجعة إلى خاص، وهو ما يخرج عن الدين والإيمان، فأبطل ذلك قولهم في دعوى العموم فيها، وألزم القول بالخصوص. فمن قضى بشيء دون شيء بلا بيان فهو متحكم. وفي ذلك لزوم قول الحسين من الوقف في جميع ما فيه الوعيد وبطلان قول من ذكر. والله أعلم.
He clarifies that with His saying: 'And whoever disbelieves in faith' the verse, and His saying: 'And whoever seeks other than Islam as a religion' the verse, and His saying: 'And whoever among you apostatizes from his religion' the verse, and upon that is the interpretation of His saying: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive association with Him' then He said: 'And He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills' [4:48]; just as He said in this: 'And We will remove from you your misdeeds' [4:31], so the bringing of one ruling is known. And it is known that there is no recourse for the Mu'tazila and Khawarij in one of them, so likewise in the other. Then the principle is that His saying: 'If you avoid the major sins which you are forbidden, We will remove from you your misdeeds' [4:31], according to the Khawarij, it is as if He said: 'If you avoid disbelief and polytheism,' and according to the Mu'tazila: 'If you avoid exiting from faith, We will remove from you what is mentioned,' so there is no major sin then according to them except exiting from faith. Thus the verse according to them becomes specific, that which removes one from religion and faith. So that nullified their claim of generality in it, and necessitated the saying of specificity. So whoever judges something without clear evidence is an arbitrary ruler. And in that is the necessity of the saying of al-Husayn of suspension (waqf) regarding everything that contains threat, and the falsehood of the one mentioned. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila and Khawarij regarding the interpretation of Quranic verses that promise forgiveness or threaten punishment. The author begins by citing several verses that indicate that disbelief and apostasy nullify deeds, and then cites the verse 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive association with Him, but He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills' (4:48) and the verse 'If you avoid the major sins... We will remove from you your misdeeds' (4:31). He argues that the Mu'tazila and Khawarij cannot have recourse to one of these verses without the other. He then explains that according to the Khawarij, the verse about avoiding major sins means avoiding disbelief and polytheism, while according to the Mu'tazila it means avoiding exiting from faith. Thus, for both sects, the only major sin that incurs punishment is exiting from faith (i.e., disbelief). This forces their interpretation to be specific, not general. The author concludes that making a ruling without clear evidence is arbitrary, and that the correct position is that of al-Husayn al-Karābisī, who held to suspension (waqf) regarding all threats—neither affirming nor denying their application to believers—while rejecting the claims of the Mu'tazila and Khawarij.

Key Terms
آيات الوعيد
المعتزلة
الخوارج
الوقف
الحسين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the Mu'tazila and Khawarij agreed on the generality of threat verses, but here the author shows their different interpretations of the condition 'avoid major sins'.
Correction: Both sects actually restrict threat to disbelief when they interpret 'avoid major sins' as avoiding disbelief or exiting faith, thereby making the threat specific.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what does the Khawarij interpretation of 'avoid major sins' imply?
A) Avoiding all sins
B) Avoiding disbelief and polytheism
C) Avoiding exiting from faith
D) Avoiding minor sins

Key Takeaway
Imam Maturidi demonstrates that the Mu'tazila and Khawarij interpretations of threat verses are self-refuting and require the position of suspension (waqf).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read verses about Allah's punishment, does your heart immediately lean towards judging others as deserving it? How does this lesson's exposure of hypocrisy in the Mu'tazila and Khawarij reveal the same tendency in yourself? What specific step will you take today to replace that judgment with reliance on Allah's mercy?
?
Think of someone you have considered 'beyond redemption' due to their sins. How does the Maturidi argument that threat verses are specific, not general, challenge your assumption? Are you willing to suspend your own verdict and leave their fate to Allah?
?
This lesson shows that even the Mu'tazila and Khawarij—despite their knowledge—contradicted themselves. Where in your own beliefs about forgiveness and sin do you hold contradictory positions? Will you settle on the humble stance of waqf (suspension) when it comes to passing judgment on others?

The Contradiction in Generalizing Promise and Threat Verses
Maturidi presents the initial contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why taking both promise and threat verses as general leads to a logical contradiction.

Core Idea
Both promise and threat cannot be absolute at the same time.

Allah promises reward for good deeds and threatens punishment for evil deeds, both in general terms. But if we take both as unconditional, what happens to a person who does both good and evil? Maturidi shows this leads to an impossible contradiction, a sign of foolishness.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening principle
Read from the beginning to 'آية السفه' and its translation. Notice that Allah's promise is without mentioning avoidance of major sins, while His threat is in general form.
The principle sets up the tension.
2
Identify the contradiction
The author says that if both are general, then combining them in one person leads to contradiction. Why? Because the same person would be both promised and threatened.
Think of a believer who commits a major sin.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
The author calls such a view 'a sign of foolishness.' Understand that this forces us to re-examine how we interpret these verses.
This sets the stage for the resolution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الأصل أن الله وعد على كثير من الخيرات وعدا من غير ذكر اجتناب الكبائر معه وأوعد على كثير من السيئات وعيدا في مخرج العموم كما وعد على الخيرات. فمن وجه الآيتين جميعا إلى العموم ألزم التناقض في جمع الأمرين في واحد، وذلك آية السفه. ثم اضطربت في ذلك الأقاويل، فزعمت المعتزلة والخوارج أن آيات الوعيد أحق بالعموم لها، إذ هو أبلغ في الزجر والموعظة. وزعمت المرجئة أن آيات الوعد أحق في العموم، لأنه أحق بالذي عرف من صفات الله من الرحمة والعفو والغفران، فتقع عن الكبائر والصغائر. مع ما يشهد لذلك قوله: إن الله لا يغفر أن يشرك به [النساء، ٤٨/٤] الآية، مع احتمال الوعيد للمستحلين. والوعد لو وجب له التخصيص ليجب لغيره، والوعيد لنفسه، فهو أولى به بالخصوص مع ما شرط الدوام ليقع الوعيد، وذلك آية الخصوص، وليس ذلك في الوعد؛ فيلزم به الصرف إلى المستحلين، أو إلى أن ذلك جزاؤه لولا الذي معه من الحسنات فيجب لديها المقابلة، أو أن ذلك جزاؤه ولله التفضل بالعفو عن ذلك، بما علم من رجائه برحمته، وعلمه بعظيم عفوه، فلا يحرمه ذلك، بما ظهر من فضله وإحسانه الذي بعثه على الرجاء - ولا قوة إلا بالله ـ أو يشفع فيهم الأخيار من عباده ويجيبهم في الاستغفار لهم، إذ يعيد الاستغفار لهم. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then the principle is that Allah promised for many good deeds a promise without mentioning avoidance of major sins along with it, and He threatened for many evil deeds a threat in the form of generality just as He promised for good deeds. So whoever directs both verses to generality necessarily entails contradiction in combining the two matters in one, and that is a sign of foolishness. Then the statements differed about that: the Mu'tazila and Khawarij claimed that the verses of threat are more deserving of generality because it is more effective in deterrence and admonition. And the Murji'a claimed that the verses of promise are more deserving of generality because it is more appropriate to what is known of Allah's attributes of mercy, pardon, and forgiveness, so they cover both major and minor sins. With what testifies to that: His saying: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive association with Him' [4:48] the verse, with the possibility that the threat refers to those who deem it permissible. And promise, if it were necessary for it to be specified, then it would be necessary for other than it, and threat is for itself, so it is more worthy of specificity along with what is stipulated of permanence for the threat to occur, and that is a sign of specificity, and that is not for promise. So it necessitates turning it to those who deem it permissible, or that that is its recompense were it not for what is with it of good deeds, then counterbalancing becomes necessary on account of them, or that that is its recompense and Allah may graciously forgive that, given what is known of hope in His mercy and knowledge of His great pardon, so He does not deprive him of that, given what manifested of His bounty and beneficence which prompted hope - and there is no power except with Allah - or the righteous among His servants may intercede for them and He answers them in seeking forgiveness for them, since He renews seeking forgiveness for them. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical argument showing the inconsistency of taking both promise and threat verses as general. The author begins by stating that Allah promised good deeds without conditioning avoidance of major sins, but threatened evil deeds in a general manner. If one takes both as general, it leads to a contradiction when the same person does both good and evil: he would be both promised reward and threatened with punishment. This is irrational. Then the author presents the positions of the sects: the Mu'tazila and Khawarij prioritize the generality of threat verses for deterrence; the Murji'a prioritize the generality of promise verses based on Allah's mercy. The author then refutes both: the threat verse about shirk (4:48) may refer only to those who deem it permissible, not all sinners. The promise needs specification because it is conditional on other factors, while threat is unconditional and thus more deserving of specificity, especially with the condition of permanence. The author then offers several possibilities for reconciling the verses without contradiction: the threat applies only to those who deem sins permissible, or it is recompense if no good deeds outweigh, or Allah may forgive by grace, or intercession occurs. The passage ends with 'there is no power except with Allah,' emphasizing reliance on divine mercy.

Key Terms
آيات الوعد
آيات الوعيد
التناقض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi identify as the consequence of taking both promise and threat verses as general?
A) They become more effective
B) They lead to contradiction
C) They support the Murji'a
D) They support the Mu'tazila

Key Takeaway
Both promise and threat verses cannot be taken as absolute generalities without leading to a logical contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a major sin, do you default to assuming God's mercy covers it unconditionally? Or do you lean towards despair, thinking His threat is absolute for you? How does this lesson expose the error in both extremes?
?
Is there a specific sin you keep committing while believing, 'God will forgive me anyway'? How does this passage challenge you to take both His promise and threat seriously, and what one change will you make this week to avoid that sin?
?
If you truly internalized that God's promise and threat cannot both be absolute, how would your daily attitude towards obedience and repentance change? What would be the first thing you would start or stop doing today?

Resolving the Contradiction: Sectarian Views and Maturidi's Synthesis
Maturidi discusses sectarian views and offers resolutions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the positions of Mu'tazila, Khawarij, and Murji'a on promise and threat verses, and how Maturidi resolves the contradiction through specification, grace, and intercession.

Core Idea
Threat verses are not absolute; they are specific to certain categories or mitigated by mercy.

After establishing the contradiction, Maturidi presents the views of the Mu'tazila/Khawarij (who favor threat verses) and the Murji'a (who favor promise verses). He then refutes both and offers a nuanced resolution that includes specification, forgiveness, and intercession.

Guided Path
1
Read the sectarian positions
Read from 'ثم اضطربت' to 'الكبائر والصغائر'. Identify the two positions: Mu'tazila/Khawarij prioritize threat verses; Murji'a prioritize promise verses.
Note the reasoning each group gives.
2
Follow the refutation
Read the rest of the passage. Maturidi refutes both extremes by pointing out that the threat verse (4:48) may be specific to those who deem shirk permissible, and that promise needs specification while threat is unconditional.
Look for the phrase 'فهو أولى به بالخصوص'.
3
Understand the resolution options
Maturidi offers several possibilities: threat applies to those who deem sins permissible, or recompense if no good deeds, or forgiveness by grace, or intercession. These resolve the contradiction without taking verses as absolute.
The passage ends with 'لا قوة إلا بالله'.

Maturidi Dismisses Al-Ka'bi's Fabrication
Maturidi dismisses a fabricated quote and refutes Al-Ka'bi's argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi exposes Al-Ka'bi's lie by showing that the Murji'ah's actual statement contradicts what Al-Ka'bi attributed to them.

Core Idea
Al-Ka'bi's quote is a lie; the Murji'ah's own words prove it.

Al-Ka'bi, a Mu'tazili theologian, tried to attack the Murji'ah by putting words in their mouths. Maturidi first dismisses this fabricated statement as worthless, then shows that even Al-Ka'bi's own logic backfires: if the Murji'ah's actual position is the opposite of what he narrated, his claim collapses. This lesson focuses on that initial dismissal and the logical refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the fabricated statement
Notice that Maturidi does not even bother to quote the fabrication because it is clearly a lie to anyone familiar with the Murji'ah's views. He dismisses it immediately as having no benefit.
This shows Maturidi's confidence in his opponent's dishonesty.
2
Understand Al-Ka'bi's argument
Al-Ka'bi claimed that the Murji'ah agreed that the grave sinner who dies unrepentant is under threat, but they differ on whether the threat is definite or possible. He then argued that this breaks consensus that such a person is not a believer.
Al-Ka'bi uses a form of argument from consensus against the Murji'ah.
3
Follow Maturidi's counter-argument
Maturidi says: if the Murji'ah's actual statement is the opposite of what you narrated, then your entire claim is invalid. He does not accept Al-Ka'bi's premise that the Murji'ah hold the view he described.
The refutation relies on the factual inaccuracy of Al-Ka'bi's description.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تكلف نصب قول للمرجئة بما يعلم كل متأمل فيه ممن قد عرف مذاهبهم كذبه فيه ليكون له سبيل الطعن عليهم تركت ذكره لقلة النفع فيه إذ هو كذب. ثم قال : إذ ثبت بمتفق القول على خلاف أحد الوعيد للفاسق إن مات قبل أن يتوب بين أهل الإرجاء، وأن يجوز أن يكون هو المعنى به ويجوز أن لا يكون إلا ما قال مقاتل: إنه من أهل الوعد لا محالة، ولا يترك لمثله الإجماع أنه ليس بمؤمن فيقال له: لو كان بالذي ذكرته يثبت الذي ادعيت. فإذ كان القول عنهم هو ضد ما حكيت يفسد ما ادعيت. ثم أكثر المنتسبين إلى الإرجاء ينكر الوعيد أن يكون في غير المستحلين معروف ذلك بينهم فهو يوضح ما ادعينا عليه من الكذب في الحكاية. والله أعلم. ثم أكثر أسئلة لا يسأل عنها ولا أجاب بأجوبة يرتضى بها من له أدنى فهم فتركتها لقلة النفع في ذكرها. والله الموفق.
He fabricated a statement for the Murji'ah, by which every contemplative person who knows their schools knows his lie in it, to have a way to attack them; I omitted its mention due to lack of benefit in it, for it is a lie. Then he said: 'Since it is established by agreed statement, contrary to one, the threat for the grave sinner if he dies before repenting among the people of irja', and that it is possible that he is the one meant and it is possible that he is not, except what Muqatil said: that he is definitely from the people of promise, and consensus is not left for someone like him that he is not a believer.' So it is said to him: 'If it were as you mentioned, what you claimed would be established.' For if the statement from them is the opposite of what you narrated, what you claimed is invalidated. Then most of those attributed to irja' deny the threat except regarding those who deem [sins] lawful; that is known among them. So it clarifies our claim of his lie in the narration. And God knows best. Then most questions are not asked about, and he did not answer with answers satisfactory to anyone with the least understanding, so I left them due to lack of benefit in mentioning them. And God is the giver of success.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Al-Ka'bi's misrepresentation of the Murji'ah's view on divine threat (wa'id). Maturidi first dismisses a fabricated statement Al-Ka'bi attributes to the Murji'ah as a lie. Then he addresses Al-Ka'bi's claim that there is agreed-upon threat for the grave sinner who dies unrepentant among the Murji'ah. Maturidi points out that the Murji'ah allow that such a person may or may not be the intended addressee of threat verses, except for Muqatil who holds that such a person is definitely from the people of promise. He then argues that if the Murji'ah's actual position is the opposite of what Al-Ka'bi narrated, his claim is invalidated. Furthermore, most Murji'ah only deny threat for those who deem sins lawful (mustahillun), which is well-known, exposing Al-Ka'bi's lie. Maturidi then notes that he omitted many of Al-Ka'bi's irrelevant questions and unsatisfactory answers due to lack of benefit.

Key Terms
مرجئة
فاسق
مقاتل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception: Al-Ka'bi's fabricated quote accurately represents the Murji'ah's view.
Correction: Maturidi shows the quote is a lie; the Murji'ah's actual position is the opposite.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi say about Al-Ka'bi's fabricated statement?
A) He considers it worth discussing
B) He dismisses it as a lie and omits it
C) He expands on it to show its errors
D) He agrees with it partly

Key Takeaway
Al-Ka'bi's attribution to the Murji'ah is false; the Murji'ah's actual view invalidates his argument.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever misrepresented someone else's view to make your own argument stronger, even slightly? How does Maturidi's outright dismissal of Al-Ka'bi's fabrication confront your own honesty in debate?
?
When you hear a claim about a group's beliefs, do you seek out their original sources to verify, or do you accept it at face value? This lesson shows that truth matters – are you willing to do the hard work to ensure you're accurate?
?
The Murji'ah leave room for God's mercy on the grave sinner. Do you have the same humility when you think about someone whose sins you find repulsive? Or do you secretly hope for their punishment?

The Murji'ah's Actual View on Threat
Maturidi clarifies the Murji'ah's actual stance on threat and dismisses further weak arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that most Murji'ah only deny divine threat for those who deem sins lawful (mustahillun), not for all grave sinners, and that Maturidi dismisses further weak questions.

Core Idea
Murji'ah deny threat only for mustahillun, not for all sinners.

After refuting Al-Ka'bi's fabricated quote, Maturidi clarifies the actual Murji'ah position regarding divine threat. Most of those attributed to irja' (the Murji'ah) do not deny threat entirely; they restrict it to those who consider sins lawful. This nuance is crucial for understanding the school. Finally, Maturidi dismisses further questions as irrelevant and poorly answered.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the actual Murji'ah view
Maturidi states that most of those attributed to irja' deny the threat only regarding those who deem sins lawful (mustahillun). This is well-known among them.
This corrects the misconception that Murji'ah deny all threat.
2
Understand 'mustahillun'
The term 'mustahillun' refers to people who consider sins lawful (halal), which is a form of disbelief. The Murji'ah affirm threat for such individuals.
Thus, the Murji'ah do not deny threat for all grave sinners, only for those who do not deem sins lawful.
3
Note Maturidi's dismissal of further questions
Maturidi says he left out many questions because they are not worth asking, and the answers given are unsatisfactory even to the least intelligent.
This reinforces that the core issue of misrepresentation has been dealt with.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

He fabricated a statement for the Murji'ah, by which every contemplative person who knows their schools knows his lie in it, to have a way to attack them; I omitted its mention due to lack of benefit in it, for it is a lie. Then he said: 'Since it is established by agreed statement, contrary to one, the threat for the grave sinner if he dies before repenting among the people of irja', and that it is possible that he is the one meant and it is possible that he is not, except what Muqatil said: that he is definitely from the people of promise, and consensus is not left for someone like him that he is not a believer.' So it is said to him: 'If it were as you mentioned, what you claimed would be established.' For if the statement from them is the opposite of what you narrated, what you claimed is invalidated. Then most of those attributed to irja' deny the threat except regarding those who deem [sins] lawful; that is known among them. So it clarifies our claim of his lie in the narration. And God knows best. Then most questions are not asked about, and he did not answer with answers satisfactory to anyone with the least understanding, so I left them due to lack of benefit in mentioning them. And God is the giver of success.

Maturidi's Refutation of an Intermediate Status Between Faith and Disbelief
Maturidi questions the proof for a wasit in names between kufr and iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument against the existence of an intermediate category (wasit) between faith and disbelief, and why he considers it an innovation.

Core Idea
God divides humanity into only two categories: believers and disbelievers.

Imam Maturidi challenges the notion that there is a third category of judgment between kufr (disbelief) and iman (faith). He argues that this intermediate status is not supported by revelation and amounts to innovation in religion. This lesson presents his reasoning and the proof he offers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the opponent's claim that an intermediate becomes necessary when the rulings of kufr and iman are removed.
Pay attention to the logical structure: claim, question, counter-argument.
2
Identify the opponent's position
The opponent (likely al-Ka'bi) posits a threefold division of judgments. Maturidi questions the basis for the third category.
This is the view Maturidi refutes.
3
Understand Maturidi's counter-argument
Maturidi asserts that God divided humans into only two categories in both worldly and religious matters. Adding a third is innovation.
He cites the Quranic verse 'among you is a disbeliever and among you is a believer' (Quran 64:2).
4
Reflect on the hadith and conclusion
The Prophet cursed those who shelter innovators; how much worse for the one who originates the innovation? Maturidi ends by seeking Allah's protection.
This shows the gravity of inventing a new religious category.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول: إذ الله يقسم الأحكام أقساما ثلاثة من حيث الانقسام من اسم الكفر، والإيمان، وما ليس بكفر ولا إيمان؛ حتى إذا زال حكم ذينك عنه لزم الواسط، فما الدليل على أن ثمة واسطاً في الأسماء؟ بل الله قسم في الجملة البشر المحتمل للعلم قسمين في أمر الدنيا والآخرة جميعاً، فمن زاد عليه فهو المبدع في دين الله ما لم يؤذن له، وقد قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من آوى محدثاً فعليه لعنة، فكيف بمن هو الذي أحدث الحدث. فنسأل الله العصمة.
Then we say: Since God divides judgments into three divisions from the perspective of division from the name of kufr, iman, and what is neither kufr nor iman; so that if the ruling of those two is removed from him, the intermediate becomes necessary. So what is the proof that there is an intermediate in names? Rather, God divided the humans capable of knowledge into two categories in the matter of this world and the Hereafter altogether. So whoever adds beyond that is an innovator in the religion of God without permission. And the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever shelters an innovator, upon him is the curse.' So how about the one who is the originator of the innovation? So we ask God for protection.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage presents Maturidi's argument against the claim that there is an intermediate (wasit) category of judgment regarding the names of kufr (disbelief) and iman (faith). The opponent (likely al-Ka'bi) posits that when the rulings of kufr and iman are removed from a person, an intermediate status becomes necessary. Maturidi questions the basis for this intermediate: what proof is there for it? He counters that God has divided people into only two categories in both worldly and otherworldly matters, as indicated by verses like 'He created you, then among you is a disbeliever and among you is a believer' (Quran 64:2). To add a third category is innovation (bid'a) in religion, and the Prophet warned against sheltering an innovator. Maturidi concludes by seeking divine protection from such innovation.

Key Terms
أحكام
كفر
إيمان
واسط
محدث
إحداث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the intermediate status is a necessary logical outcome of removing the rulings of kufr and iman.
Correction: Maturidi shows that this contradicts the explicit Quranic division of humanity into only two categories, and therefore is an innovation.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the problem with claiming an intermediate (wasit) in the names of kufr and iman?
A) It contradicts the Quranic division into two categories (kufr and iman).
B) It is supported by hadith.
C) The intermediate is only for the major sinner (sahib al-kabira).
D) The intermediate is only for the hypocrite (munafiq).

Key Takeaway
Adding a third category between faith and disbelief is an innovation not supported by Scripture.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever considered yourself or someone else as 'in between' faith and disbelief? How does Maturidi's argument challenge that comfortable middle ground, and what is the danger of inventing categories God did not?
?
The Prophet warned against sheltering an innovator; how often do you passively accept religious ideas that have no clear basis in the Quran and Sunnah? What is one innovation you need to confront in your own thinking?
?
God divides people into only two categories: believer and disbeliever. If someone asked you today which you are, would you answer with certainty? Why or why not? What does this passage demand of you right now?

Refuting the False Intermediate: Maturidi's Critique
Maturidi refutes the opponent's proof for an intermediate status using Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of the opponent's proof from Quranic verses for an intermediate status, and how he affirms the Quranic category of the hypocrite as the true intermediate.

Core Idea
The Quran's only intermediate is the hypocrite, not the major sinner.

Maturidi engages with an opponent who uses selective Quranic verses to claim an intermediate religious status for the major sinner. In this passage, Maturidi exposes the flaw in that reasoning by showing that the verses are misapplied and that the Quran itself already defines a clear intermediate group: the hypocrites. This lesson will guide you through his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the structure: the opponent's argument is stated, then Maturidi's critique follows.
The passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the opponent's argument
The opponent uses verses that seem to exclude the major sinner from being a disbeliever (fighting/jizya verses) and from being a believer (glad tidings verses). Understand why this suggests an intermediate status.
3
Understand Maturidi's first counterpoint
Maturidi points out that for those who consider the major sinner a believer, glad tidings are conditional or refer to the end, not a present status. This undermines the opponent's use of those verses.
4
Grasp Maturidi's second counterpoint
Maturidi notes that even the Khawarij, who see the major sinner as a disbeliever, do not apply a uniform ruling (execution/jizya) to all disbelievers—showing the opponent's logic is inconsistent.
5
Recognize the Quranic intermediate
Maturidi concludes by citing the Quran's own threefold division: believers, disbelievers, and hypocrites. The hypocrites are the true intermediate, negating the need for a separate status for the major sinner.
This is the key doctrinal point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتج بما ليسوا بكفرة بآيات قتال الكفرة وأخذ الجزية ونحو ذلك، وبما ليسوا بمؤمنين بآيات البشارة والولاية ونحو ذلك؛ فبهذا خرج عن جملة قول المؤمنين. كأنه أغفل عن جملة أخرى لهم، وهو أن البشارة عند من يرى صاحب الكبيرة مؤمنا كانت بشريطة أو كانت هي العاقبة. وعند الخوارج كان الحكم في الكفرة على نوعين أحدهما على القتل أو أخذ الجزية، والآخر لا، كالنساء وأهل النفاق ونحوهم. فمن رام أن يجعل ثمة واسطا في الأحكام - بما هي عند الفريقين يلزم لا بما ذكر من الواسط - أغفل عن جملة قول الأمة. ولا قوة إلا بالله. ما كان الله تعالى قد بين الأقسام الثلاثة الكفرة والمؤمنين وأهل النفاق، وهم المذبذبون بينهما، وأخبر أنهم ليسوا من هؤلاء ولا من هؤلاء. فمن رام تثبيت الواسط، لا على ما جاء به النص، وأراد أن يجعله مقابلاً له، على نفي الحقيقة التي جعل الله لها الواسط، فقد ضيع حقوق القسمة ونقض الترتيب الذي جاء به القرآن فاستوجب المقت به من جميع منتحلي الإسلام. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And he argued using [verses that they are] not disbelievers by verses of fighting the disbelievers and taking jizya and the like, and that they are not believers by verses of glad tidings and guardianship and the like; thus he departed from the totality of the saying of the believers. As if he neglected another totality of theirs, which is that glad tidings, according to one who considers the major sinner a believer, were conditional or were the outcome. And according to the Khawarij, the ruling regarding the disbelievers was of two types: one is execution or taking jizya, and the other is not, like women and the hypocrites and the like. So whoever intends to make an intermediate in the rulings - as they are according to the two parties, it becomes necessary, not by what was mentioned of the intermediate - he neglects the totality of the saying of the ummah. There is no power except with Allah. Allah the Exalted has indeed explained the three categories: the disbelievers, the believers, and the hypocrites, who are wavering between them, and He informed that they are not from these nor from those. So whoever intends to establish the intermediate, not according to what the text came with, and wants to make it opposite to it, by negating the reality for which Allah made the intermediate, then he has wasted the rights of division and violated the order that the Quran came with, and thus deserves hatred from all the followers of Islam. There is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage contains Maturidi's refutation of the opponent's (al-Ka'bi) proof. The opponent used Quranic verses that treat the major sinner as not a disbeliever (e.g., verses about fighting disbelievers and taking jizya) and not a believer (e.g., verses of glad tidings and guardianship) to argue for an intermediate status. Maturidi points out that the opponent ignored two important points. First, for those who consider the major sinner a believer, glad tidings are either conditional or pertain to the final outcome, not a present status. Second, the Khawarij themselves divide the rulings for disbelievers: some are killed or pay jizya, others (women, hypocrites) are not. Thus, the opponent's attempt to establish an intermediate based on these verses is flawed because he neglects the full scope of the ummah's positions. Moreover, the Quran itself already defines the true intermediate: the hypocrites (munafiqun), who are wavering between the two groups. Anyone who tries to establish a different intermediate that contradicts the Quranic division loses the proper classification and merits condemnation.

Key Terms
كفرة
مؤمنون
منافقون
مذبذبون
واسط
قسمة
جزية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The opponent's use of Quranic verses is a valid basis for positing an intermediate status for the major sinner.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the verses are misinterpreted and that the Quran's own intermediate is the hypocrite, not the major sinner.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the true intermediate (wasit) mentioned in the Quran?
A) The major sinner (sahib al-kabira).
B) The hypocrite (munafiq).
C) The one who commits minor sins.
D) The people of the book.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi refutes the claim of a separate intermediate status for the major sinner by showing the Quran's only intermediate is the hypocrite.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you label someone as 'not really a believer' because of their sins, are you unintentionally inventing a category that the Quran never authorized? How can you align your judgments with the Quran’s clear division of people?
?
Maturidi warns that neglecting the Quran's classification deserves hatred from all Muslims. Is there an area in your life where you have been redefining what Allah has clearly divided, such as mixing truth with falsehood? What step will you take today to submit to His categories?
?
The hypocrites are the only intermediate—they waver. Have you ever wavered in your commitment to faith due to fear of people or love of this world? What specific situation challenges your steadfastness, and what verse can you cling to in that moment?

Dismissal of the Objection Based on the Case of the Woman
Maturidi dismisses an objection based on the woman as an exception, asserting that disbelief rulings are not uniform.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi dismisses the objection regarding the woman as an invalid analogy and why rulings of disbelief cannot be generalized from exceptional cases.

Core Idea
The woman's case is an exception, not a proof for an intermediate status.

In this passage, Maturidi addresses a specific argument his opponent raises about a woman who commits a major sin. The opponent claims this case is an exception (makhsus) that proves an intermediate status between faith and disbelief. Maturidi firmly rejects this reasoning and explains why such analogies are invalid.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its English translation. Notice how Maturidi uses strong dismissive language.
The passage is short but packed with meaning.
2
Identify the opponent's claim
The opponent claimed that the woman is an exception (makhsus). What did they hope to prove by this? Think about the doctrine of an intermediate status.
Maturidi calls this type of reasoning 'fantasy'.
3
Understand Maturidi's response
Maturidi argues that rulings of disbelief are not uniform, so one case cannot be used as evidence. He also criticizes the opponent's extensive but failed attempts to refute the Khawarij on this point.
This shows his methodological rigor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم عارض نفسه بالمرأة فزعم أنها مخصوص. وهذا النوع من الخيال، بل أحكام الكفر مختلفة لا يستدل بها على شيء. وقد رأيته أطنب في معارضات الخوارج، وتكلف الخروج مما قابلوه به، مما يعلم كل من تأمله أنه لم يحقق ما رام إلزامه، ولا تخلص مما قوبل به حق التخلص، فأغضيت عن ذكرها.
Then he objected with [the case of] the woman and claimed that she is an exception. And this type is of fantasy. Rather, the rulings of disbelief are different and cannot be used as evidence for anything. And I saw him expound at length in the refutations of the Khawarij and straining to escape from what they confronted him with, such that everyone who ponders knows that he did not achieve what he intended to oblige, nor did he extricate himself from what he was confronted with in a true extrication, so I turned away from mentioning them.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage briefly addresses an objection the opponent raised concerning the case of a woman who commits a major sin. The opponent claimed that this woman is an exception (makhsus) to the general rulings, implying that an intermediate status exists. Maturidi dismisses this as a fantasy, arguing that the rulings of disbelief are diverse and cannot serve as a basis for generalization. He notes that the opponent went into lengthy and forced attempts to refute the Khawarij on this point, but ultimately failed to achieve a convincing refutation or to escape their objections properly. Therefore, Maturidi chooses not to engage further with these specious arguments.

Key Terms
امرأة
مخصوص
كفر
خوارج
معارضات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The example of the woman proves that there is an intermediate status between faith and disbelief.
Correction: Maturidi explains that rulings of disbelief are diverse and cannot be generalized from a single case; the woman does not provide evidence for an intermediate status.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi reject the objection based on the case of the woman?
A) Because women are not subject to rulings of kufr.
B) Because rulings of kufr are not uniform and the example does not prove an intermediate.
C) Because the Khawarij agree with him on this issue.
D) Because the woman is a hypocrite.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi dismisses the woman analogy as irrelevant because the rulings of disbelief are not uniform and cannot be proven by exception.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face an objection to your faith or practice, do you tend to make excuses or rely on exceptional cases to avoid the full implication of the ruling? How can you instead submit to Allah's diverse rulings without rationalizing?
?
Maturidi criticizes the opponent for straining to escape from objections. In your own life, have you ever twisted arguments to defend a comfortable belief rather than humbly accepting the truth? What is one area where you need to stop defending and start submitting?
?
The rulings of disbelief are not uniform and cannot be generalized from a single example. Are you quick to judge others' faith based on one action? How can you cultivate a more nuanced understanding of people's iman, recognizing that Allah alone knows the true state of the heart?

Refutation of Denying Iman to the Major Sinner
Maturidi refutes an opponent who removes the name of iman from a major sinner.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's refutation of those who deny the name of iman to a major sinner, and the charge that such denial amounts to slandering Allah.

Core Idea
Denying iman to a major sinner is slander against Allah's own naming.

Imam Maturidi here delivers a powerful rebuttal to an opponent who argues that a person committing a major sin no longer deserves the title 'believer'. He challenges the opponent's motive and accuses him of audaciously contradicting Allah's own designation. This passage is a direct and polemical defense of the broad nature of iman.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Notice the direct address and strong language.
2
Identify the two scenarios
Maturidi presents two possible motives for the opponent: if it's for his own self, that's his choice; but if he denies iman to others, he is slandering Allah. Find these two scenarios.
3
Understand the charge of slander
Maturidi argues that the opponent's denial contradicts Allah's naming of believers in the Quran. Reflect on why this is considered slander.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيقال له : إن كان جهدك في صرف اسم الإيمان عن المبتلى بكبيرة ـ على ما فيه من تعظيم الرحمن وخشية العواقب - لئلا تُسمى أنت به فلك ما اخترت في نفسك وسويته؛ وإن كان ذلك لتزيل هذا عن غيرك فهو يعلم جرأتك في ذلك على الله بما فهم من تسمية الله إياه بغير الذي سميته، فلا يُحتمل أن يرتاب في خبر الله ـ مع ما يعلم من نفسه كذلك ـ بافترائك على الله بتسويل الشيطان. ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثم الذي ذكرته لا يحتمله إلا سفيه : أن يقول ويعاتب على ما يعلم كذبه فيما يعاتبه عليه . فأما الله سبحانه الذي لا يخفى عليه شيء يتعالى عن الرتبة التي يأنف منها كل ذي لب . والله المستعان . وأما أنت فحقيق لذلك، لأنك تيأس به من روح الله وتؤثر بشهوتك عداوة الله وولاية الشيطان وتتعرض في مذهبه لمقته ولعنه. فهنيئاً لك ما اخترته لنفسك عند الكريم والرحيم. ولا قوة إلا بالله .
It is said to him: If your effort in removing the name of iman from the one afflicted with a major sin — despite what is in that of magnifying the Most Merciful and fearing consequences — so that you are not called by it, then you have what you chose for yourself and equated; and if that is to remove this from others, then He knows your audacity in that against Allah because of what you understood from Allah's naming him with other than what you named him, so it is not possible that he doubts the report of Allah — while he knows from himself likewise — because of your slander against Allah through the whisper of Satan. And there is no power except with Allah. Then what you mentioned is not borne except by a fool: that he says and rebukes what he knows is false in what he rebukes him for. As for Allah the Exalted, from Whom nothing is hidden, He is exalted above the rank from which every possessor of intellect would disdain. And Allah is the Helper. And as for you, you are deserving of that, because you despair through it of the mercy of Allah and prefer through your desire the enmity of Allah and the friendship of Satan, and you expose yourself in his path to His wrath and curse. So congratulations to you for what you chose for yourself with the Generous, the Merciful. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 452

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an opponent (likely Al-Ka'bi) who argues that a person committing a major sin does not deserve the name 'believer'. Maturidi first addresses the opponent's motive: if he does this out of reverence for God and fear of punishment for himself, then that is his own choice. But if he tries to deny the name to others, then he is audaciously contradicting Allah's own naming of such persons as believers in the Quran. Such a person cannot be trusted, as he slanders Allah. Maturidi then calls the opponent a fool for rebuking based on what he knows is false. He contrasts Allah's exaltedness with the opponent's lowly state, accusing him of despairing of mercy and siding with Satan. The tone is harsh and polemical.

Key Terms
اسم الإيمان
المبتلى بكبيرة
افتراء
ولاية الشيطان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that major sins negate iman entirely, so a major sinner is no longer a believer.
Correction: Maturidi insists that God's naming of believers stands; denying iman to a major sinner contradicts divine naming and is slander.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi accuse the opponent of doing by denying iman to the major sinner?
A) Following the Quran literally
B) Slandering Allah by contradicting His naming
C) Showing excessive mercy
D) Neglecting worship

Key Takeaway
Maturidi refutes the denial of iman to major sinners by charging the opponent with slandering Allah and contradicting divine naming.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a fellow Muslim committing a major sin, do you ever silently remove the name of 'iman' from them in your heart? How does Allah's naming of them challenge your own judgment—and what does that say about your view of His mercy?
?
Maturidi charges the opponent with despairing of Allah's mercy. Is there any sin so great in your eyes that you think its doer is beyond hope? What does that reveal about your trust in Allah's attribute of mercy—and are you willing to repent from that despair today?
?
The opponent's desire to distance himself from sinners is labelled as 'siding with Satan.' In what specific ways might your own pursuit of righteousness lead you to separate yourself from those you consider sinful, rather than seeing them as fellow believers under Allah's mercy? Will you ask Allah to forgive your pride and grant you a heart that mirrors His compassion?

Maturidi's Refutation of the Mu'tazila on Minor Sins
Maturidi reports and refutes the Mu'tazila view on minor sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazila claim that persistence on minor sins makes them major by redefining persistence and appealing to Quranic distinctions.

Core Idea
Persistence is not continuing a sin but refusing to repent.

The Mu'tazila argued that repeatedly committing a minor sin without repentance elevates it to a major sin requiring eternal punishment. Maturidi challenges this by clarifying what 'persistence' really means and showing how it contradicts clear Quranic distinctions. In this passage, he redefines the term and exposes the logical consequences of their position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise argumentative style of Maturidi.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila position
What exactly do the Mu'tazila claim about minor sins and persistence? Locate their statement in the first sentence.
They say persistence turns a minor sin into a major one.
3
Understand Maturidi's redefinition
Maturidi argues that persistence is not continuation of the act. Find his definition of persistence and note how he supports it.
He equates persistence with abandoning repentance and regret.
4
Follow the refutation
See how Maturidi uses the Mu'tazila's own logic to show that their position contradicts Quranic verses that distinguish between types of sins.
This reveals the theological error in their claim.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider the ultimate implication: if all sins require repentance to avoid eternal punishment, then minor sins would lead to eternity, contradicting clear Quranic distinctions.
This shows the soundness of Maturidi's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قالت المعتزلة : صاحب الصغيرة إذا أصر عليها يصير صاحب كبيرة. والإصرار على ذلك الفعل ليس هو لزومه، لأنه لا فعل يمكن لزومه حتى لا يتحول منه إلى غيره. فليس إذا الإصرار إلا ترك التوبة والندامة عليه، وكل الذنوب من الشرك وغيره مغفور بالتوبة عنها والندامة عليها. فيبطل على قولهم حق هذه الآية من التفصيل بين الشرك وما دونه، وحق الآية الأخرى من التفصيل بين الكبائر وما دونها، ويحصل القول على أن كل ذنب يوجب الخلود إلا أن يتاب عنه، وذلك بين لمن تأمله ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then the Mu'tazila said: The owner of a minor sin, if he persists upon it, becomes an owner of a major sin. And persistence upon that action is not its continuation, because there is no action that can be continued such that he cannot turn away from it to something else. So persistence is nothing but abandoning repentance and regret over it, and all sins, from shirk and other than it, are forgiven by repentance over them and regret over them. So according to their statement, the right of this verse of detail between shirk and what is below it is invalidated, and the right of the other verse of detail between major sins and what is below them, and the statement results that every sin necessitates eternity unless one repents from it, and that is clear for whoever contemplates it, and there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage reports the Mu'tazila position that persisting in a minor sin elevates it to a major sin. Maturidi refutes it by redefining persistence: it is not mere continuation (since one can always cease), but the refusal to repent and regret. Thus, under their view, all sins require repentance to avoid eternal punishment (khalud). This, however, contradicts the Quranic distinction between shirk and other sins, and between major and minor sins, showing the inconsistency of their claim.

Key Terms
صغيرة
كبيرة
إصرار
توبة
خلود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Persistence on a sin means simply continuing the same action repeatedly without interruption.
Correction: Maturidi teaches that persistence is not the continuation of the act, but the abandonment of repentance and regret for that sin.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the correct definition of 'israr' (persistence) on a minor sin?
A) Continuing the action without interruption
B) Abandoning repentance and regret
C) Committing the sin publicly
D) Intending to sin again

Key Takeaway
Maturidi refutes the Mu'tazila by showing that their view on persistence leads to contradictions with the Quranic distinctions between major and minor sins.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a minor sin, do you immediately turn to Allah in repentance, or do you let it slide? How does Maturidi's definition of persistence challenge your usual view of 'just a small sin'?
?
If every sin requires repentance to avoid being held accountable, how seriously do you take the act of saying 'Astaghfirullah'? Does your regret match the weight of your actions?
?
Which of the Quranic distinctions (shirk vs lesser sins, major vs minor) do you typically ignore in your daily life? What would it cost you to repent from those neglected areas right now?

Is Every Sin Obedience to Satan? Unpacking a Dangerous Whisper
An opponent argues that every sin is obedience to Satan; Maturidi warns it is a whisper.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that all disobedience is obedience to Satan is a dangerous whisper (waswasa) that can lead to disbelief, and how Imam Maturidi refutes it.

Core Idea
Not every act Satan loves is obedience to him; intention and command matter.

This passage presents a subtle theological trap: if every sin is what Satan desires, then every sinner is obeying Satan. Imam Maturidi warns that this argument is not for mainstream theological factions but for those vulnerable to whisperings (waswasa). He shows that accepting it would ironically make one obedient to Satan and a disbeliever.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Carefully read the opponent's argument: every opposition to God is something Satan calls to, so why is it not obedience to him?
The opponent equates any sin with obedience to Satan.
2
Identify Maturidi's response
Note how Maturidi redirects the question: it is not for Khawarij/Mu'tazila but for those suffering from whisperings (waswasi). He warns that accepting this argument leads to disbelief.
Maturidi dismisses it as a whisper that traps the vulnerable.
3
Reflect on the danger
Consider how accepting the argument could make one an obedient follower of Satan, and why this is a tactic of Satan to cause disbelief.
The cure is recognizing it as a whisper and seeking Allah's protection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال قائل : إذ كان كل خلاف الله فهو مما دعا إليه الشيطان ويسر به لو فعل، لم لا صار ذلك طاعة له ؟ ومن فعل فعلا لطاعة الشيطان يكفر أو يصير به عابدا له، إذ ذلك منه وضع شرع مقابل لشرع الله ودعوة إليه. ومن عبد الشيطان فقد بين الله منازل عبّاد الشيطان. قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : نقول : ليست هذه المسألة للخوارج والمعتزلة، لإقرارهم في الأنبياء بالزلل ،والأخيار، لكنها لبعض الموسوسين، يوسوس إليهم الشيطان هذا ، ليكفرهم بهذا؛ إذ ذلك معلوم أنه من تزيين الشيطان وما دعا إليه هو ، فيصيرون على قولهم مطيعين له كفارا ، نسأل الله العصمة عنه.
And a speaker said: Since every opposition to God is from what Satan calls to and delights in if done, why is that not obedience to him? And whoever does an act for the obedience of Satan becomes a disbeliever or thereby becomes a worshipper of him, because that is from him placing a law opposed to the law of God and a call to it. And whoever worships Satan, God has made clear the stations of the worshippers of Satan. Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: We say: This question is not for the Khawarij and Mu'tazila, because of their affirmation of prophets' slips and the righteous, but it is for some of the waswasi (ones who get whisperings), to whom Satan whispers this, to make them disbelieve through it; since that is known to be from the adornments of Satan and what he calls to, so they become, according to their statement, obedient to him and disbelievers. We ask Allah for protection from it.
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage presents a rhetorical objection: if every sin is what Satan loves, then every sin is obedience to Satan, leading to disbelief and worship of him. Imam Maturidi responds by dismissing this as irrelevant for Khawarij and Mu'tazila (who accept prophetic errors), but identifies it as a dangerous whisper (waswasa) from Satan aimed at making people disbelieve. Those who accept this argument would, ironically, become obedient to Satan and disbelievers.

Key Terms
طاعة (obedience)
عبادة (worship)
شيطان (Satan)
وسوسة (whispering)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that any act Satan loves is automatically obedience to him, ignoring the role of intention and command.
Correction: Maturidi shows that this reasoning is a whisper from Satan that leads to disbelief; true obedience requires conscious intention and command.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, who is most vulnerable to the argument that all disobedience is obedience to Satan?
A) The Khawarij
B) The Mu'tazila
C) Those who suffer from whisperings (waswasa)
D) The righteous

Key Takeaway
Imam Maturidi teaches that the claim that every sin is obedience to Satan is a dangerous whisper, not a valid theological position.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that a single sin makes you completely obedient to Satan, as if you have betrayed Allah entirely? How does Maturidi’s warning that this very thought is a whisper from Satan change how you should react to that feeling? Commit to reminding yourself that your sins do not define your loyalty to Allah unless you embrace that false equivalence.
?
When you sin, do you immediately despair of Allah’s mercy, thinking you have become like a worshipper of Satan? Maturidi says that accepting such reasoning leads to disbelief. How can you train yourself to reject that whisper and instead turn to repentance without losing hope? What specific step will you take the next time this thought crosses your mind?
?
Picture a brother or sister in faith who is struggling with guilt over a sin they keep repeating. They tell you, ‘I feel like I am obeying Satan every time I sin.’ Using the exact terms from this lesson, how would you warn them against that dangerous whisper without dismissing their struggle? Write down what you would say.

Faith Is in the Heart, Not the Tongue
Maturidi proves that faith is located in the heart, not the tongue.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Maturidi locates faith in the heart rather than the tongue, based on the heart's essential role in activating good deeds and validating worship.

Core Idea
Faith resides in the heart because only the heart can validate worship.

Maturidi begins by challenging the view of the Karramiyya, who held that faith is a bodily act. He then presents a theological argument: Allah has placed the highest degree of faith in hearts, making hearts the source of good deeds and the validator of worship. This passage establishes the internal nature of faith as a matter of the heart, not mere verbal confession.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its literal translation. Notice the flow and key terms like الكرامية, الإيمان, القلب, اللسان.
The passage is dense—pause after each sentence.
2
Identify the opposing view
Maturidi begins by refuting the Karramiyya. Think about what the Karramiyya might have believed that is being rejected here.
The Karramiyya held that faith is a bodily action or verbal confession.
3
Understand Maturidi's proof
Maturidi argues that Allah raised the degree of faith in hearts, making hearts the instrument for good deeds and the condition for valid worship. Why can only hearts bear this?
Focus on the logical link: faith enables good deeds and worship; only hearts can do that.
4
Grasp the conclusion
Maturidi concludes that hearts are more worthy (of being the seat of faith) than tongues. Reflect on what this implies about the nature of faith.
This passage is a clear statement of the centrality of inner conviction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثبت أنه على غير ما ظنت الكرامية. على أن الله تعالى أعلى درجة الإيمان في القلوب حتى صيّرها أعلى الدرجات، وصيّر الإيمان مما يقوم به الخيرات؛ وعند وجوده يصلح العبادات؛ وما يحتمل ما وصفت إنما هو القلوب لا الألسن، لذلك كانت أحق.
It is established that it is not as the Karramiyya thought. Indeed, Allah Almighty raised the degree of faith in hearts until He made them the highest degrees, and made faith that by which good deeds are performed; and when it exists, acts of worship are valid; and what bears what I have described are only hearts, not tongues, therefore they are more worthy.
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage presents a proof that faith (iman) is essentially in the heart, not the tongue. The author begins by refuting the view of the Karramiyya, who held that faith is a bodily affirmation. Then he argues that Allah has elevated the degree of faith in hearts, making hearts the locus for performing good deeds and validating acts of worship. He concludes that only hearts can bear this description, not tongues, so hearts are more deserving of being the seat of faith.

Key Terms
الكرامية
الإيمان
القلب
اللسان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think faith is simply verbal confession without inner conviction.
Correction: Maturidi shows that faith must be in the heart because only the heart can produce good deeds and validate worship, which no number of words can accomplish.

Checkpoint
Why does Maturidi argue that faith is in the heart rather than the tongue?
A) Because the tongue can be used for both truth and falsehood
B) Because the heart is the seat of understanding and acts of worship are dependent on it
C) Because the Karramiyya said so
D) Because the tongue is not mentioned in the Quran

Key Takeaway
Maturidi establishes that faith is a matter of the heart, not the tongue, because only the heart can be the source of righteous deeds and the validation of worship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Where does your faith truly reside—in your heart or only on your tongue? When you perform good deeds, is it because your heart is alive with iman, or are you just going through the motions? How can you ensure that your heart is the source of your worship?
?
Consider your own acts of worship. Do you feel that they are validated because your heart is convinced, or do you sometimes find your tongue moving while your heart is absent? What would change if you truly internalized that faith is in the heart?
?
The Karramiyya thought faith was a bodily confession. Are there areas in your life where you have reduced faith to external actions without inner conviction? What would it look like to bring your whole heart into those areas?

Sinners Retain the Name of Faith Despite Rebuke
Maturidi refutes those who remove the name of faith from sinners using Quranic rebuke verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses Quranic verses and rational analogy to argue that sinners retain the name of faith despite their shortcomings.

Core Idea
Faith remains even with sin; Allah rebukes believers as believers.

Imam Maturidi addresses a critical debate in early Islam: does committing a sin remove one from faith? While some groups like the Khawarij declared sinners disbelievers, Maturidi points to Quranic verses where Allah rebukes believers while still addressing them as believers. This lesson examines those verses and the rational argument that follows.

Guided Path
1
Identify the refuted groups
Read the passage and list the four groups Maturidi refutes: Mu'tazila, Khawarij, Karramiyya, and Hashwiyya. Notice that they all have different doctrines but share the idea of removing the name of faith from sinners.
2
Examine the Quranic verses
Take note of the four Quranic verses Maturidi cites. Each verse addresses the believers directly while rebuking them for a shortcoming. Observe that Allah does not stop calling them 'belivers' despite their failure.
The verses are from Surah 61, 9, 4, and 57.
3
Grasp the rational analogy
Maturidi gives an analogy from everyday life: friends rebuke each other for shortcomings, while enemies fight and argue. Since Allah's rebuke is like that of a friend, it confirms that the relationship of faith remains.
4
Understand the conclusion
The passage concludes that the name of faith remains with sinners, thus nullifying the positions of those who expel from faith or declare disbelievers. This is the key point of the lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي هذا النوع آيات هي تنقض على المعتزلة والخوارج والكرامية والحشوية مذهبهم على اختلاف مذاهبهم نحو قوله: يا أيها الذين آمنوا لم تقولون ما لا تفعلون... وقوله تعالى: يا أيها الذين آمنوا ما لكم إذا قيل لكم انفروا في سبيل الله... وقوله تعالى: وما لكم لا تقاتلون في سبيل الله والمستضعفين... وقوله تعالى: ألم يأن للذين آمنوا أن تخشع قلوبهم لذكر الله... فعاتب عز وجل على صنيعهم ذلك وأعظم الوعيد في ذلك، ولم يزل عنهم اسم الإيمان بل به عاتبهم وكذلك في العقل المعاتبة بالتقصير يكون بين الأولياء، ويكون بين الأعداء محاجة ومحاربة. فبان أن قد بقى لهم اسم الإيمان، فيبطل قول من يُخرج من الإيمان وقول من يُكفره.
And in this category are verses that refute the Mu'tazila, Khawarij, Karramiyya, and Hashwiyya in their doctrines, according to their different schools, such as His saying: 'O you who believe, why do you say what you do not do' (61:2-3), and His saying: 'O you who believe, what is the matter with you that when you are told to go forth in the way of Allah' (9:38), and His saying: 'And what is the matter with you that you do not fight in the cause of Allah and for the oppressed' (4:75), and His saying: 'Has the time not come for those who believe that their hearts should be humbled for the remembrance of Allah' (57:16). So He, Exalted, rebuked them for that action and made great the threat in that, yet He did not remove from them the name of faith; rather He rebuked them by it. Likewise in reason, rebuke for shortcomings occurs between friends, while between enemies there is argument and war. So it became clear that the name of faith remains with them, thus nullifying the saying of those who expel from faith and those who declare them disbelievers.
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of those who claim that committing major sins removes one from faith entirely (such as the Khawarij) or makes one a disbeliever. Maturidi cites several Quranic verses where Allah addresses believers who are failing to do what they should—such as not fighting in jihad or not humbling their hearts—and yet He still calls them 'believers.' The rebuke itself is directed at them as believers, not as non-believers. In human affairs, friends rebuke each other for shortcomings, while enemies fight. So the fact that Allah rebukes them with the name 'believers' proves that they still possess faith. This invalidates the position of those who remove the name of faith from sinners or declare them disbelievers.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
الخوارج
الكرامية
الحشوية
اسم الإيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Committing a major sin removes a person from the faith entirely, making them a disbeliever or outside the fold of Islam.
Correction: Maturidi shows that Allah addresses sinners as 'believers' in the Quran and rebukes them, which proves that the name of faith remains even with sin. Only actions that constitute apostasy can remove faith.

Checkpoint
What point do the Quranic verses about rebuking believers serve in Maturidi's argument?
A) That believers never sin
B) That sins remove the name of faith
C) That believers are rebuked as believers, so faith remains
D) That only the tongue matters

Key Takeaway
Allah's rebuke of believers as believers shows that sin does not remove the name of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you still consider yourself a believer? Or do you feel that your faith is completely lost? What does this lesson teach you about your identity in times of failure?
?
If Allah rebukes believers as believers, how does that change the way you view your own shortcomings? Will you now receive His rebuke as a friend or as an enemy?
?
The lesson says rebuke between friends is different from enemy confrontation. How do you respond when Allah's commands challenge your desires? Do you react as a friend who accepts correction, or as an enemy who fights back?
